Free Talk

A Laughing Matter

— Seafarer

A: Why did you open three holes in the wall?

B: So that our three kittens can go in and out.

A: Then one hole is enough.

B: Where did that come from? If there was one cat, of course, one hole would be opened. Now there are three cats, so there must be three holes.

A: My grandfather is ninety-five years old this year.

B: What's so rare about that? My grandfather is one hundred and twenty years old this year.

A: Such longevity is truly a national treasure. May I meet him?

B: Then I'll have to dig up the ancestral grave.

A: Life is like a train running on tracks. If it derails, there is danger.

B: What analogy do you have for a husband and wife?

A: For example, two train cars are connected and moving forward.

B: Then what is someone like me, an old widower, like?

A: Like a train that isn't connected and is coldly left aside.

A: Why does Old Bing always eat in front of a mirror?

B: He's very frugal. Eating a dish of vegetables in front of a mirror is like eating two dishes.

A Short Stay at Mogan Mountain (6)

— Jingbo

Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government organized the Mogan Mountain Management Bureau, many municipal constructions have been carried out in the mountains. Electric lights and telephones have been installed one after another. The mountain roads operated by foreigners have been unconditionally handed over to Chinese management after serious negotiations. Although the foreigners' summer resort can continue to exist, its influence has declined and it is unable to interfere in mountain administrative affairs. In the past, foreigners mostly privately transferred property in the mountains, and the contracts were not perfect. After the establishment of the Management Bureau, it was stipulated that foreigners should not own property in the mountains. If foreigners want to sell real estate, they can only sell it to Chinese people. Therefore, in the past one or two years, Chinese villas have been increasing day by day. Generally, the foreigners' residences are in extremely good locations, and when they are sold, the room's utensils and appliances are given as gifts. Recently, people have been buying houses from foreigners from time to time. It is expected that in less than ten years, there will be no foreign residences in the mountains, and Mogan Mountain will become a perfect summer resort for Chinese people.

The railway hotel's catering methods are the same as those on sea ships. In addition to the three meals, tea and snacks are provided to guests in the early morning and afternoon. Meals are also served at fixed times. However, it is impossible to have snacks outside of these times, because it is not easy to buy food in the mountains. If you want to share a meal with guests at the hotel, you must inform them in advance, otherwise there will be no way to respond at the last minute. I think that in the future, more people climbing the mountain will bring canned food for occasional needs. I stayed in the mountains for a few days and occasionally saw something, so I wrote it down in a jumble, and I didn't feel that the words were wasteful. (End)

A Record of the Filial Son of Kong's Tomb

— Wang Meiju

Yesterday, after getting drunk at the home of my friend Wu Liuyi, I returned to Seymour Road. Because it was not far away, I walked under the cloudy sun. When I reached the corner of Xinza Road, I suddenly heard someone calling from behind. When I looked back, an old man in a rickshaw bowed to me and said, "Are you not Wang Shuchen?" (My old name was Shuchen, and few Shanghai friends know it.) "Do you remember Xu Zigu, a friend from Suzhou in those years?" I also said, "I haven't seen you for forty years, no wonder I don't recognize you when we meet." So I invited him to sit down at Baimeting Pavilion. We talked about what had happened since we parted and asked about each other's recent situation. Zigu said, "I don't know where to start with a Twenty-Four Histories. But now that I have met you, you are good at ancient prose, so you should write a biography for the Filial Son of Kong's Tomb." I didn't know what to say, so Zigu solemnly narrated it. The filial son's surname is Cheng, and he is a fisherman from Kuatang Bridge, Suzhou. He lost his parents when he was young and lived with his aunt, Ms. Zhang. When he was young, although he had entered a village school, he was fond of playing and knew few words. His aunt was a fisherman, so Cheng followed her to play with nets. Later, he married a woman named Hong, and his aunt died without an heir. Cheng and his wife observed mourning for her like a filial son. Whenever they got fish, they must present it in three cases in front of the thatched cottage, saying, "To sacrifice to my parents, aunt, and teacher Confucius." People laughed at him for being unethical. Hong also said, "Why does a fisherman worship Confucius?" Cheng didn't listen and did it every day without getting tired. Ten days ago, after setting up a sacrifice, he went in to sell fish. At noon, he cried and returned home, holding a piece of cloth and ordering Hong to cut it into a waist belt. He and his wife and two children put on mourning clothes on the boat. His wife was at a loss, and the neighboring boats also changed their color to explore. Hong said, "My family has no great merit from either the husband's or the mother's family. I don't know what he is doing today." Cheng cried bitterly and didn't hear his wife's answers to people. After a long time, many people persuaded him to stop and asked him who was dead. Cheng beat his chest and cried to the sky, "The great sage of China for thousands of years will now destroy his tomb! How can I not cry?" Everyone seemed to understand or not, and some suspected that he had some kind of stimulus or neurological disorder. However, from that day on, he cried morning and evening until Zigu left Suzhou last night. He had not stopped for seven days. Meiju said, "This is better than Duo Duo, the filial son of Xuanling in the Han Dynasty." Zigu also said, "Recently, I heard that a woman wrote to the National Government to remove the ancient books so that only the Three Principles of the People would exist in the world. However, the fisherman is destroying Confucius' tomb as if he had lost his parents. Why do they each go to extremes?" I can't name the mystery. I have briefly recorded the ins and outs of this matter and call him the Filial Son of Kong's Tomb.

The Naming of Lu Gaojian

— Qiulang

The meat shops at sea compete to hang the "True Lu Gaojian" brand. At first, I didn't know what it meant. Recently, while chatting with a friend, I asked him about it. My friend said, "According to legend, there was a man from Suzhou named Lu who set up a meat shop in the market. Although he worked in the slaughter industry, he was naturally kind and often gave to the poor. One day, a beggar came to the shop, emaciated and ragged. Lu gave him money, but he didn't accept it. He wanted a corner of the house to shelter him from the wind and rain. Lu took pity on him and agreed, giving him a straw mat to use as a bed and giving him food every day without being stingy. After living there for more than a month, the beggar's illness had healed. He bid farewell to Lu, saying, "I am grateful for your kindness, but I have no way to repay you. Please use this straw mat as fuel to cook meat to show my heart." Lu did as he said. Suddenly, the meat in the pot emitted a strange fragrance that spread far and wide. People came to buy it, and his life became prosperous. Therefore, the meat shop brands all used this good name.

Can Fish Hear?

— Qiushui

The question of whether fish have hearing organs and can hear human speech and movements has long been the center of discussion for ichthyologists. There have always been two theories. Anglers, for example, is famous for advocating that fish have hearing organs. However, general zoologists say that although fish have ears, they cannot use them, severely criticizing the absurdity of his theory. The two sides have been arguing until now. Can fish hear? It is indeed a very interesting question, so I will list the latest theories on the left.

Listening to Music to Discriminate Food Recently, a scientist named Herr HStertte at the University of Maulik in Germany wrote an article published in major newspapers in Berlin to support Anglers, saying that fish can hear the sound of music. The basis for this is his years of field experiments. He said that he had kept various kinds of fish at home. When feeding them, he must mix them with music or various human voices every day. After a long time, when the sound wave was made, even without food, the fish's hearing was very sensitive. He first used a certain sound to represent a kind of high-quality food and then used another sound to represent a kind of inferior, inedible thing. After training on time for a long time, when the fish heard a certain sound, they gathered together. When they heard other sounds, they were indifferent and did not move. Therefore, the fish not only have hearing organs and can listen to music, but also their hearing is sensitive and they can also listen to the sound and discriminate food.

Fish Have No Ears However, those who hold the opposing view are actually numerous. A zoology expert in London once told a newspaper reporter, "I have done various experiments with animals in the zoo, and I do not believe that fish can hear as Mr. Stette said. If you hide yourself beside the fish tank and clap your hands to make a sound, the fish will swim in the tank as usual without moving. However, if you stand facing the water and clap your hands again, the fish will gather together and float on the surface of the water to ask you for food. Therefore, I believe that fish have sensitive vision and touch, but there is definitely no such thing as hearing."

Fish Can Distinguish Colors Although there are still doubts about whether fish have hearing organs and can listen to and distinguish sounds, the fish's vision is extremely sharp and has already become a recognized fact. Try to use a red plate to serve high-quality food to feed them, and at the same time use a blue plate to serve inferior food to give them. After a long time, when the fish see the red plate coming, they gather together and scramble for food. They are indifferent to the blue plate and do not move. Alas, fish are also spiritual things!

Barefoot Movement

— Tao Zaidong

In this scorching summer, compelled by social obligations, one cannot avoid making visits. As a member of the "long gown" faction, it is impossible not to wear silk socks and satin shoes. During this time, I feel a sense of suffering because, since falling ill, I have been confined to my home, spending the summers barefoot for the past three years. This year, starting from the old Dragon Boat Festival, I have been bareheaded and barefoot for two months. Once I have to wear the long gown and socks, I feel like I am in shackles, as hot as being burned, and all kinds of discomfort affect my whole body. It is not until this moment that I realize the joy of being barefoot. Thinking back to the thirty years of bustling about in famous places, falsely claiming to play a role, running around in officialdom with hand plaques and boots, suddenly all eight feet are suspended in the air, and the roasting feet are unbearable. In short, the right to be barefoot has been sacrificed for a long time, and I deeply regret and cherish this motive for my "Foolish Barefoot Movement". I plan to designate the period from the beginning of summer to the beginning of autumn as the barefoot period every year, regardless of who it is, everyone will be barefoot, but other clothing will remain the same, whether wearing a long gown or a suit and formal dress, but with bare feet, wouldn't it be unsightly? The response should be that it will be normal once people get used to it. What is so unsightly? Hands are solid proof that wearing a long gown or suit without gloves and with bare hands is not unsightly. Bare feet are even more acceptable as long as people get used to seeing them. This movement, I also plan to expand from bare feet to bare chests, and from bare chests to being naked. The civilization faction often criticizes being bare-chested as barbaric, but the foreigners use sunbathing as treatment, so it becomes civilized. Being naked has theories such as the "model of truth, goodness, and beauty" as its basis. Considering that the timing is not yet ripe for the latter two aspects, I will postpone them for now and start with being barefoot, which has three benefits. First, bare hands and bare feet ensure equality between hands and feet, preventing discord and laying the foundation for overall freedom. Second, it is convenient. Washing feet is much easier than wearing socks, and the sweat and odor are greatly reduced, which is beneficial to hygiene. Third, it is free. The money saved from buying socks during this movement period averages one yuan per person, which amounts to 40,000 yuan, a significant economic benefit. Fellow countrymen, why not join us? After drafting this article, I saw a newspaper report that Marilyn, a female star from Hollywood, is advocating a "no socks" movement and practicing being barefoot, which is indeed the same as my own idea. However, in China, I am still a pioneer in being barefoot.

News from the Art World: Mr. Huang Zhuan Tao, a novelist from Wumen, is skilled in painting. He previously collaborated with Mr. Yu Yifen on fan pages, which were frequently requested. Now, Mr. Huang has set a gifting method. The cost is two yuan, and the fan surface will also be gifted by Mr. Huang. For local customers, items will be collected in three days; for customers outside of the city, items will be mailed in two days. The collection address is Xin Shanghai Tongxun She, No. 18, Block B, Baker Road, Shanghai.

Eastern Travel Impressions (27)

— Qian Hua

During the elevator ride, the driver does not rest for a moment, speaking with utmost politeness and humility. Therefore, "dōmo" is continuously used fluently and pleasantly ("dōmo" is the most polite ending in Japanese). At each elevator entrance, the greeters bow to ninety degrees when opening and closing the elevator's iron gate to show welcome and farewell, while telling guests the classification and advantages of the goods displayed on the floor, echoing the driver in perfect harmony. These women have undergone considerable training by the company, first taught mechanical knowledge and then taught response phrases, so that they can use them skillfully once put into practice. A joker said that the driver is like a nightingale, and the elevator is a birdcage, with the clear sound of the nightingale reaching the ears, fulfilling the passengers' shallow desires. The ages of the drivers and greeters at Matsuzakaya are younger, from eleven or twelve to fourteen or fifteen, which makes them seem even more lively and cute. In addition to elevators, department stores also have escalators, which allow customers to reach the third, fourth, and fifth floors without lifting a foot, and there is no limit to the number of people. One can easily ascend the steps and ascend quickly, which is more convenient than elevators. There are also customer lounges and rooftop gardens, arranged in an elegant and serene manner. The lounges offer tea and cigarettes to guests, and the women are attentive in their hospitality. One does not need to make a purchase to be entitled to this. The rooftop garden is filled with flowers and trees, and contains exotic goldfish. Looking down from a high vantage point, the entire city of Tokyo is clearly visible. Whenever the sun sets in the west, the visitors seem to weave together. There is a dining room in the garden that sells all kinds of food at affordable prices, and it is often crowded. There are also several young girls hired next to the main entrance of the Matsuzaka star, who specialize in welcoming and sending off customers. Mitsukoshi employs young children to do this, constantly holding perfume bottles and spraying them on customers to show respect. As for the internal layout, every effort is made to attract customers' attention, such as Mitsukoshi's Far East Games special room, which displays photos, medals, and records of previous games, as well as prizes from all walks of life in this session, such as Chiang Kai-shek's silver pagoda and this newspaper's silver shield, all arranged in a dazzling array. Other events, such as Matsuzakaya's cosmetics conference and Marubishi's hot spring exhibition, are also sufficient to increase public knowledge and arouse keen interest. What makes us feel infinite emotion is that nineteen of the goods sold in department stores are made in Japan, and only one or two are imported, and are only used as decorations. Their prices are incredibly high, while our country is the opposite. The wealth of national power is determined by this.

Eastern Travel Correspondence (16)

— Wu Xiaohou

The revival of Tokyo is a major undertaking. At 11:58 a.m. on September 1, 1923, the great earthquake in Tokyo was an unprecedented catastrophe in Japan's history. Japan was built on a volcanic mountain range, and minor earthquakes have been seen many times, but such an earthquake that destroyed Tokyo's more than 500 years of culture, factories, and all buildings, except for a part of the Japanese Imperial Palace, and at the same time, more than 80 fires broke out in the city, destroying everything into scorched earth for two days and nights, was a rare sight. According to the statistics, the total area of the 15 districts in Tokyo is 77.48 million square meters. Except for Ushigome Ward, the area affected by the disaster in the remaining 14 districts is about 34.6 million square meters. The number of buildings burned down is 219,000, the number of households is 366,000, and the population affected by the disaster is 1,484,000. The estimated damage is 3.7 billion yen, which is about 20 times the area burned down and 37 times the damage amount of the famous Great Fire of London in 1666 AD, which can be called a major disaster that is only seen in ancient and modern times.

After the great earthquake, Japan suffered great pain. The government and the public unanimously took measures to provide relief and recovery. The Japanese government established a recovery bureau in the Ministry of Interior to plan and implement the national recovery plan, such as the construction of main roads, the construction of canals, the establishment of large parks, the reorganization of land zoning, the subsidization of building costs in fire-prevention zones, and other small projects as government recovery facilities (government recovery facilities cost about 336.987465 million yuan). In addition, the Tokyo Prefecture Facility (Tokyo Prefecture Recovery Facility costing approximately 22.004036 million yuan) will revise national roads, construct ring and radial roads, and educational facilities. The Tokyo City established a city recovery bureau to plan and implement the recovery work of the entire city. Here, we will select key items to explain in detail.

(1) City Land Zoning Reorganization: The entire implementation area of Tokyo's land zoning reorganization covers 65 districts. In addition to the 15 districts with government facilities, the city facility area covers 50 districts. The reorganization cost is approximately 93.951 million yuan.

(2) Subsidy Line Road Construction: The subsidy line roads are built in succession to the main line roads. The total number of routes is 122, with an extension of 139,146 meters. The construction cost is approximately 82.111994 million yuan.

(3) Road Surface Paving and Bridge Reconstruction: Road surface paving and bridge reconstruction for the restoration and reconstruction of damage and new construction caused by the Great Earthquake includes 715,473 square meters of road surface paving, of which 400,554 square meters are newly built. There are also 154 bridges, of which 53 are newly built. The cost of paving and reconstruction is approximately 12.45332 million yuan. (4) Sewer Improvement: The first and second phases of sewer facilities were damaged by the earthquake. The cost of reconstruction and improvement of facilities, as well as the remaining works of the first and second phases, and the newly emerging works of the third phase, is approximately 40.211321 million yuan.

Commercial News

Financial and Gold Markets Trend from Strong to Weak

Different Opinions Among the Trade

Yesterday, the gold market situation on the eighth turned from strong to weak. However, the trend was still sensitive and the attitude was hesitant, making it difficult to grasp the real intentions.

The market showed no intent to move forward. The forward market had a total of five taels in review, and the after-market contained an ambush of six taels. In general, the bulls were pushing up, while the bears were suppressing slightly, with mutual restraint. Foreign exchange seemed slightly loose. Dealers' transactions varied. Yuan Maoyong, Yongfeng, Fuchang, and hedgers were all buying in. Taikang Runyu, Dayi Fengyong, etc., had all sold out. Hengxing Zhifengyong, etc., had varying demands. In the morning, large transactions were inactive and still stable. Later, buyers surged and gradually increased prices. At noon, it reached 84 taels. Afterwards, Hengxing bought Zhifengyong, Yuan Maoyong, Taikang Runcheng, Fengyong, etc., who mostly sold their positions. Initially, the positions were still strong, but then exchange rates weakened and dealers' minds softened. The market sentiment changed from sharp to weak. It plummeted four or five taels, and finally broke through the 80-tael mark, a stark contrast to the previous day. Yesterday, banks and exchange rates remained unchanged.

Morning Market Gradually Increases

The gold price for September was 580 taels and 0.06 mace, with each tael priced at 0.03 mace. The gross spread fluctuated by 1.2 taels. It once reached 79.34 taels, but then the shorts sold again. Subsequently, the buyers rose and gradually increased by 2.3 taels to 82.1 taels. However, exchange rates seemed weak. September gold for England could be settled at 6 pence 625. Hanzhou Financial Situation Amidst Turbulence

According to news from the financial sector yesterday, the financial situation in Hanzhou is currently very critical. All kinds of agricultural products from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River are often interrupted because transportation cannot be fulfilled as desired. The losses to silver interest warehouses cannot be overstated. Currently, the minimum monthly interest rate for every 1,000 taels of Zhuang interest in Hanzhou must be over 20 taels of silver. If the buying and selling of Shanghai standard silver drafts is compared to spot transactions, the distance is always 8 or 9 taels, and at least over 7 taels. If the two deliveries at the end of the 15th of the month are often offset by telegraphic transfers, the losses are even greater. Currently, the foreign exchange funds are about 20 million, and are mostly stored in various banks and cannot be used as circulating market funds. Therefore, the market is very short of spot funds. Although there are banknotes in circulation, the selection criteria are very strict, and several types of Shanghai banknotes cannot be used.

New York, 7th - The first U.S. government cotton harvest report is scheduled to be released on the 8th. Based on estimates from various private institutions, the forecast is 66.5% of the normal annual output, totaling 14,190,000 bales.

Grain and River Rice Prices Fall Back

Zhabei

Yesterday, the number of suppliers arriving from various gangs was small, only a few. Sales in this street were stagnant. However, rice merchants with factory-produced rice and boat rice were quite eager to sell. Therefore, the North Rice market situation softened. High-quality short-grain rice and medium to low-quality rice all fell by two to three jiao. Moreover, buyers were scarce. The real reason is that new Kunshan rice has been successively entering the market and will arrive in Shanghai soon. Furthermore, every day, 400 to 500 shi of new Nanjing indica rice have been arriving. Most buyers are going directly to Nanjing to purchase. Sales in Shanghai are therefore poor, so the atmosphere in the market is unusually depressed. Although the supply of Dongxin rice is exhausted, it has also softened by two to three jiao. Top-quality goods have fallen to around 21 yuan. The overall average is only between 20 yuan 0.5 and 0.6 jiao. The arrival of thin rice is still scarce. The market situation is stable. Sales of flexible rice are balanced. High-quality rice is still priced at 19 yuan.

South Shanghai

Few boats are coming down the river, and sales are lackluster. Top-quality rice from the Chang gang continues to decline. Sales of Suzhou-Tong white rice are poor, and the price is slightly soft. Sharp Decrease in Autumn Silkworm Rearing in Japan

Sales of Japanese raw silk to Europe and the United States are sluggish. Silk inventories are growing daily, and there is an overproduction. In order to adjust the silk market, the Japanese government is reducing the amount of autumn silkworm rearing. The second and third sleeps for autumn silkworms in each county is already here, and on average, the amount of rearing has been reduced by 50% compared to last autumn.

Rice Market

South Shanghai

Yesterday, at the market located at No. 34 Luli Road, the appetite was limited. Dealers from Suzhou and Tongzhou quoted 2 jiao more. Early and late rice, as well as Yangdujian rice, were scarce in the market. Yesterday, 130 shi of newly harvested粳 rice from Zhoupu arrived, and the market price dropped by half a yuan compared to the previous trading day. The current market prices are listed below:

Local News

China Merchants Bureau’s All Inland River Vessels Chartered by Zhejiang Navigation Affairs Bureau

All Inland River Vessels Resume Service

The number of inland river shipping companies in Shanghai in recent years, the sluggishness of business, and the difficulty of navigation along the route are unprecedented. Upon investigation, the foreign merchants operating inland river vessels in Suzhou, Hangzhou, and other places include Daishengchang and Datong, two Japanese firms, and Laogongmao, a British firm. Several years ago, business was very good, and the British and Japanese vessels all made great profits. However, in recent years, business has declined, and Japanese merchants have taken the opportunity to transfer Daishengchang to Chinese merchants and renamed it Yuantong. Datong has also been taken over by Chinese and renamed Qingji, while the Japanese, carrying their huge profits, have returned to their country fully loaded. Among inland river vessels, China Merchants Bureau has always occupied the first position in terms of business volume. Its routes cover Jiangzhe and the inland, and its ships and transportation are also larger than Daishengchang and others. However, in recent years, due to unrest in the inland, difficulty in navigation, limited cargo and passengers, and the increasing number of small companies, it has become difficult to sustain. As a result, China Merchants Bureau's inland river vessels have suspended operations, and inland waterway transportation has also been affected. This year, since the Zhejiang Construction Department established the Navigation Affairs Bureau, it has been striving to develop inland river transportation in the province. It has negotiated with China Merchants Bureau to charter all of the bureau's inland river vessels that have been largely suspended, and the Zhejiang Provincial Government has dispatched personnel to take over management. The charter agreement has been signed, and shipyards and other items have also been received. A formal plan is now being drawn up to fully restore all of the vessels that have been suspended for a long time. The details of this matter are recorded as follows:

Navigation Affairs Bureau Committee Takes Over

The Zhejiang Navigation Affairs Bureau has chartered all of China Merchants Bureau's inland river vessels and has changed the Shanghai Suzhou Road General Bureau into the Shanghai Branch Bureau. A general management office has been established in Hangzhou, Zhejiang. The Navigation Affairs Bureau has specially appointed Chen Shuntong, a specialist in Shanghai shipping, as the general manager, and Sheng Nian as the deputy manager. Zhang Shusheng has also been appointed as the manager of the Shanghai Bureau. The name has been carefully determined as the Zhejiang Provincial Navigation Affairs Bureau's Chartered China Merchants Inland River Vessel Bureau. The charter agreement was signed in mid-June, and Mr. Chen and Mr. Sheng have already taken office. Recently, they have come to Shanghai to negotiate with the former bureau chief regarding the takeover of the bureau's ships, docks, tugs, and other matters. Since the first of this month, the entire operation has been under the command of the new general manager and others.

Twenty-One Inland River Routes Resume Service

After taking over the bureau's affairs, Mr. Chen and Mr. Sheng have decided to restore all of the routes that have been suspended for a long time. In recent days, they have been in contact with various ports in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces to discuss the resumption of navigation. As of yesterday, the new bureau has formulated a plan to resume navigation on the following routes: 1. Shanghai-Hangzhou route, 2. Shanghai-Suzhou route, 3. Changli route via Wantazhai, Qiaozhai, Xushe, etc., 4. Xili route via Luoshe, Yixing, Yun Village, 5. Xicheng route via Qingyang, Tongcheng Township, 6. Shanghai-Jiaoze route via Huangdu, Qingpu, 7. Shanghai-Lingze route via Luxu, Pingwang, Shengze, 8. Shanghai-Huzhou route via Lili, Zhenze, Nanxun, 9. Suzhou-Dangze route via Nanqiao, Ganlu, 10. Suzhou-Changzhou route via Zhangjiatian, 11. Suzhou-Shengze route via Wujiang, Beichi, Xincheng, 12. Suzhou-Huzhou-Hangzhou route via Linghu, Xu Dian, Tangxi, 13. Xun-Jia route via Meiyan, Wangjiangjing, 14. Jia-Hu route, 15. Zhenjiang-Yangzhou-Guazhou route, 16. Zhen-Qing route via Yangzhou, Shaobo, Huaicheng, 17. Zhenjiang-Xiaohe route via Hejing, Hehuachi, Sanjiangtai, Tianxingqiao, 18. Xiashi-Haining route, 19. Changshu-Qingyang route, 20. Changzhou Butou route, 21. Changzhou Yangxiang route.

Independent and Transparent Accounting

The new bureau will eliminate previous malpractices and adopt a policy of integrity. Accounting will be independent. The bureau's accounting director will be Jiang Zhongxun, specially appointed by the Construction Department. All income and expenditure will be made public, and monthly reports will be submitted to the Navigation Affairs Bureau. The basic capital of the new bureau will be allocated by the Construction Committee.

Preliminary Organization of Operations

A total of twenty-one ships were received, plus twenty-one company ships. Among them was the "Jian Yuan" ship, which burns diesel fuel and is the latest model. The rest burn coal. Chen Shengjun is a specialist in the shipping industry. The most important aspect of ship operation is fuel consumption. Previously, round trips on the Shanghai-Hangzhou route required twenty tons of coal. Now, with Chen Sheng et al. personally supervising combustion and using higher-quality coal, each round trip only burns nine and a half tons. This could save over ten thousand yuan on coal for the twenty-one ships per month. In July, Chen Sheng and the other gentleman received the ships and test-operated them for a month. After expenses, they actually made a profit of three to four thousand yuan. Therefore, the new bureau believes there is a real possibility of reorganization and revitalization. The new bureau has now decided to maintain the current state of the routes within Jiangsu Province and gradually develop them, starting with expanding operations on the routes within Zhejiang Province.

Extension of Land Registration in Jiangsu Province for Three Months

Land registration in Jiangsu Province began on February 10th of this year and was originally scheduled to end on August 9th, a period of six months. The deadline has now passed. Registration matters in various counties have largely been delayed and neglected, resulting in no progress. However, the counties have repeatedly stated to the provincial authorities that due to disasters and famine in the past year, bandit and communist disturbances, or military influences, they have been unable to carry out the work effectively. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has now decided to extend the deadline for three months from August 10th to continue the work. Within this deadline, the counties must urge all districts to earnestly expedite the registration. If the deadline is exceeded again, those with verified deeds will be required to pay a fee, and those without verification will be fined double. Yesterday, the Shanghai County Government received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs to comply.

British Warship Carries British Troops to Hankou Yesterday

For the Purpose of Protecting Overseas Chinese

The "Great American Evening Post" reports that the British warship HMS "Whitehall" was ordered to Shanghai from Weihaiwei and arrived at the Wusongkou this morning (August 8th). It immediately loaded the second batch of fifty British soldiers and set off for Hankou. These British soldiers were waiting in Songjiang in advance and will join the 110 soldiers who departed yesterday on the "Xiang He" steamship and be stationed on warships to protect overseas Chinese.

Japanese Warship Collides with British Steamer

The Japanese destroyer "Kashi" was traveling from Shanghai to Hankou yesterday when it collided with a British steamer near Wusongkou. Both sides were unable to give way in time, and the bow of the "Kashi" struck the hull of the British steamer. The bow of the Japanese ship sustained only minor damage, while the hull of the British steamer was damaged. It came to Shanghai yesterday for repairs, while the Japanese ship continued to Hankou.

The Municipal Government Promotes the New System of Weights and Measures

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Complies with Orders to Promote

And Displays a Full Set of New Instruments

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce received an order from the Municipal Government yesterday stating that the promotion of the new system of weights and measures depends on the publicity of the system, so that the general public can deeply understand the benefits of the new system and the drawbacks of the previous lack of uniformity. Currently, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has already produced and commissioned the Shanghai Zhonghua Book Company to publish real-life pictures of new instruments, comparison charts of the new system, and uniform procedures for the new system nationwide. The work has now been completed. Therefore, the Ministry is allocating and sending copies to the provincial and municipal governments for distribution to various agencies for publicity, examination, and verification. The Chamber is ordered to comply and widely publicize the system. If the aforementioned charts are insufficient, they can be purchased directly from the Zhonghua Book Company. After receiving this order, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has already displayed a full set of Ministry-approved new weights and measures at the Commodity Exhibition Hall for public viewing.

Hunanese Refugees to Receive the Press Today

Dozens of refugees from Hunan Province arrive in Shanghai every day. They plan to provide a detailed account of the Changsha Incident to the public and have scheduled a reception for the press today.

Wang Zhengting Arrives in Shanghai Last Night

Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting left Beijing at 12:00 noon yesterday on the express train to Shanghai and arrived at 9:25 p.m. that evening.

Mr. Lei Bingyang Returns to Songjiang

Mr. Lei Bingyang, the former Chargé d'affaires to Sweden, returned to Shanghai from Europe a few days ago. He originally planned to go to Beijing immediately, but he caught a cold on the way and is unwell. Therefore, he will first return to Songjiang to recover for a few days before going to Beijing.

Statistics on Exports to the United States in July

According to the "China Press," the U.S. Consulate General estimates that Shanghai's exports to the United States in July totaled US$2,806,444. The total for the first seven months of this year is US$26,917,492. Textiles and their raw materials still accounted for the largest share of exports in July, with a value of US$2,099,341, nearly three-quarters of the total export value. In addition, inedible plant products were valued at US$256,344, and inedible animal products were valued at US$219,264. The rest were negligible, only tens of thousands of U.S. dollars. In July, Shanghai's exports to the Philippines were valued at US$157,342, and the total for the first seven months of this year was US$1,584,516. Exports to Honolulu were valued at US$6,030, and the total for the first seven months of this year was US$7,745.

Therefore, he sent a letter inviting the heads of districts 1236 to discuss ways to improve communication. However, only the heads of districts 2 and 3, Peng Lire and Yang Fulin, attended yesterday. Director Wu discussed the matter with them. Because this matter requires joint discussion by all districts, it was decided to reschedule the meeting.

The Beima Section of the County Telephone System Begins Operation

The Overall Plan for the County Telephone System is Being Drafted

The long-distance telephone project for the Beima section of the county has been completed. A few days ago, Wu Wenhua, Director of the County Construction Bureau, personally went to inspect and test the telephones and requested the Construction Department to send personnel for acceptance inspection. According to Director Wu yesterday, the project's results are very good. Non-official calls have begun in recent days as a trial and are not charged. The local people are competing to use them and feel very convenient. The regulations for telephone management and charging in this section have already been drafted and have now been approved by the county government and filed. The instructions from the Construction Department have not yet arrived. Formal calls will be implemented after the Department's acceptance inspection, charged at five cents per call. In addition to the installation of one telephone in Beima and another in Ruanjiazhai, two telephones are installed in other places for now due to funding issues. More will be added when the project develops in the future. After all district telephones in the county are fully installed, it will be even more convenient. A new plan is being drafted and will be completed soon.

Commemorative Stamps of Revolutionary Martyrs

To Be Issued Soon

Wang Boqun, the Minister of Transportation, specially prepared to print and issue a commemorative stamp of revolutionary martyrs for the sake of commemorating revolutionary martyrs, and distributed it to the postal administrations of various provinces and cities to replace the stamps currently circulating on the market. Now it is learned that the model of the stamp has been specially made by the American Art Company and sent to Shanghai. Wang has reviewed it and is quite satisfied with the result. The Social Affairs Bureau Requests the Customs to Abolish the Lunar New Year Holidays

The Social Affairs Bureau stated that the central government has long ago issued orders and regulations for the promotion of the national calendar. The settlement periods for merchants and various festivals have also been recalculated and determined. However, it is heard that the Jianghai Customs in this city still has various lunar calendar holidays in its official holidays and closing dates, such as three days of annual leave from the first to the third day of the first lunar month, one day of summer festival leave on the fifth day of the fifth lunar month, and one day of autumn festival leave on the fifteenth day of the eighth lunar month. Customs is a national tax authority. If it continues to use the lunar calendar, it will not only confuse people's perceptions but also hinder the promotion of the national calendar. It has sent a letter to the Superintendent of Public Affairs to inform the Jianghai Customs to abolish various lunar calendar holidays and change to complying with the national calendar.

The French Water and Electricity Labor Strike - Latest News

General Meeting of Members

Yesterday afternoon at 3 p.m., a general meeting of members was held at the public sports field. More than 1,300 people attended. Zhang Amao presided over the meeting. The Municipal Party Department sent Wu Jiaze to attend and provide guidance. The Second District Public Security Bureau sent Inspector Gao and 20 armed police officers to maintain order. First, the chairman reported on the progress of the mediation. Then, the following resolutions were discussed and decided: (1) Send Tang Zihe and six others to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for punishment. (2) If the labor strike is not resolved, all workers should take appropriate action. (3) Strictly investigate union spies and lackeys who have infiltrated the union to gather information and hold the inspection team responsible for strict investigation. (4) Require the factory to not dismiss workers without reason after resuming work. (5) Do not resume work until the goal is achieved.

Meeting of Staff Members

Yesterday morning at 10 a.m., a meeting of staff members was held, attended by more than 200 people. (Omitted below)." A letter of thanks was immediately sent. Xu Amei reported that the workers were obeying discipline and waiting quietly for a resolution.

Departure to Solicit Donations

Yesterday, the Nanhua Goods Industry Union sent personnel to join the French Water and Electricity workers to start soliciting donations from the members of the industry. The members of the support committee also set out to solicit donations to maintain the spirit of the strike.

Workers at Xiang Sheng Factory Request Rice Subsidy

Can be Resolved in One or Two Days

Workers at the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong, recently raised the issue that rising prices of goods have affected their livelihood. Therefore, they resolved at a general meeting a few days ago to request the factory to increase the rice subsidy by two yuan per person per month on the 5th of this month. The Municipal People's Training Committee had previously approved this matter. Zhang Linhua, the standing committee member of the committee, entered the factory and consulted with the general foreman Peng Si and the second foreman Yang Balo. The factory indicated its willingness to accept the request and promised to increase the monthly rice subsidy by one yuan for each worker. However, Zhang indicated that the current request was the lowest limit of the labor side and could not be conceded. The two sides negotiated for a long time. Finally, the factory agreed to investigate the price of rice since June and seek the consent of the board of directors, promising to reply within three days before dismissing the meeting. Yesterday, the three-day period had expired. The factory management sent a letter to Zhang to negotiate again. The negotiations lasted a long time and had not been completed by 5 p.m. It is said that the factory management is quite aware of the suffering of the workers, so the request is unlikely to cause problems and can be resolved in about one or two days.

Craftsmen at the Railway General Factory Request Rice Subsidy

Craftsmen in all departments of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway General Factory previously received orders to give those with monthly salaries of 51 yuan to 100 yuan a housing subsidy of 5 yuan 1 dime. Therefore, workers with general monthly salaries below 50 yuan specially elected Cai Jinhai and Tang Ziliang, the standing committee members of the trade union, as representatives to petition the superiors to request a rice subsidy. It has been approved that those with monthly salaries below 30 yuan will be given a rice subsidy of 11 yuan, to be paid when the July salary is issued on the 5th of this month. However, workers with general salaries above 30 yuan to 50 yuan expressed dissatisfaction because they received nothing. While they were discussing this, those who had already been promised a housing subsidy of 5 yuan 1 dime were also unhappy because they had not yet received the money. They gathered at the writing room to question the clerk Xiao Xiyang, who was in charge of the worker's accounts. Wang Chengzu, the Director of the Traffic Department, found out and came forward to dissuade them and promised that the housing subsidy of 5 yuan 1 dime per person would be issued to the workers below 50 yuan on Friday (yesterday). The workers then put forward the condition that the price of 12 yuan per stone of rice be taken as the standard. If the market price is 15 yuan per stone, a rice subsidy of more than 3 yuan will be added, and the subsidy will be calculated according to the increase in the market price. Director Wang of the Traffic Department agreed to report the situation to Director Liu for review and ordered the workers to return to the workshop to work as usual and await news. The crowd then complied and retreated.

The Issue of Disposing of the Two-Line Pension Fund

The Traffic Department of the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau issued a notice to all employees of the lines yesterday, stating that Luo Panhui, the document committee member of the Two-Line Pension Fund, wrote to the effect that the two-line pension fund and the subsidy fund have now accumulated to more than 1.7 million yuan, most of which is deposited in various banks. Recently, the financial sector has been affected by high gold prices, and there have been moments of alarm. The fund is the capital of the workers' blood and sweat, and the relationship is very important. Article 21 of the Detailed Rules of the Association states that a part of the subsidy can be invested in reliable and profitable industries, but the investment method should be studied publicly to ensure stability. Therefore, a letter is specially sent to you and ask your director to forward it to all employees for their opinions on this matter. Please collect all opinions and reply by August 15 for a meeting to discuss and select the best option. In addition, it is heard that most of the two-line workers intend to ask the Traffic Department to investigate and distribute the money, as the current situation is causing high prices and high cost of living during the national crisis.

The Sino-Japanese Labor Strike Is Still Difficult to Resolve

Workers at the Rihua Cotton Mill in Pudong previously demanded a 10 cent increase in the rice subsidy from the factory management because of the high cost of living. They also demanded the cessation of Sunday night work and the elimination of intentional wage delays. It has been many days since then, but the two sides have been unable to reach an agreement. According to a reporter from Huadong News Agency yesterday, the union said that when the matter was raised, the management agreed to consider it. However, the attitude suddenly changed the next day, and the management went from a moderate to a tough stance and posted a notice at the factory gate, stating that it had received a letter of accusation from all the workers, accusing the workers Yu Qixiang, Gu Lanru, Ren Nianxi, Bu Linsheng, Hu Shoulin, Pu Xiangyun, and Wang Zhaozhu of instigating the incident. Therefore, the seven workers were publicly dismissed, and other workers were asked to resume work. The wording was groundless, but fortunately all the more than 4,000 workers were not moved. Therefore, the factory is still unable to resume work. However, as the delay has been prolonged, the workers' livelihoods are likely to be affected. Therefore, plans are being made in recent days. Yesterday, the Municipal Party Department was petitioned to remain calm and await the Municipal People's Training Committee and the Social Affairs Bureau. The reporter then went to the factory to investigate. The factory gate was locked. Only a Chinese official and Japanese guards were inside. When asked if the foreman Inoue was there and if there had been any news recently, they said that the foreman had not been to the factory for many days. The factory headquarters was in Caojiadu, and there had been no similar incidents. Therefore, the shipment of goods had not been affected. It seemed that they were absolutely unwilling to compromise on the strike.

Jinpu and Longhai Borrow Money to Pay Salaries

The Jinpu and Longhai lines have borrowed 100,000 yuan from the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo lines to pay part of their salaries as a result of reduced revenue due to the war, which has caused the salary to be delayed for three to five months.

Minutes of the Municipal Citizens' Union Meeting

Eight Important Cases Were Resolved

The Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Union held its seventh plenary meeting yesterday afternoon. More than 20 committee members attended. Zhang Yichen presided over the meeting. The secretary reported on the minutes of the previous meeting and various telegrams. Then, the following proposals were discussed: (1) The joint association of tenants in Ruikang Lane, Hongkou, sent a letter and dispatched two representatives to the meeting to report that the landlord, the Yeguang Company, was exceptionally harsh and requested assistance. It was decided to forward the three requirements put forward by the association to the Yeguang Company to uphold justice. (2) Lu Wenzhong sent a letter requesting a protest against the Public Works Bureau for piling up garbage in various places, hindering the health of the people of the city. It was decided that the matter was of concern to the interests of all citizens within the boundary and would be handed over to the Investigation Section for detailed investigation before sending a letter to the Chinese Director to protest. (3) Wu Jianguang and others from Nanjing Road requested assistance for the matter of the landlord digging up the house. It was decided to hand it over to the Investigation Section for investigation and then review it. (4) Should condolences be paid for the death of committee member Chen Wenbin due to illness? It was decided that the association would send condolences and members would make their own donations. (5) Committee member Wang Pingnan proposed that Fuzhou merchant businesses request assistance from foreign insurance companies who are attempting to evade insurance compensation. Wang Pingnan proposed the following measures: (A) Petition the central government to order foreign insurance companies in various places to register with the Public Works Bureau, otherwise they will not be allowed to operate. Chinese merchants should not be allowed to insure with unregistered foreign insurance companies, otherwise they will not be accepted in the event of a dispute. Committee member Jiang Xinzhao proposed that, based on the facts of this case, the association should issue a declaration to notify all Chinese merchants to switch to Chinese insurance companies to avoid being deceived by foreigners and suffering losses. It was decided to pass this resolution. (6) The regulations for the organization of the Rice and Grain Special Committee were submitted for discussion. It was decided to ratify them as originally written. (7) Committee member Yu Yangsheng reported that Zhang Maocheng Rice Shop in Haining Road sold rice at a fair price to relieve civilians. Should the association commend them? It was decided that the association would send a letter of commendation. Other proposals were discussed at the end of the meeting before it adjourned.

Minutes of the Joint Meeting of Representatives of Pharmaceutical Associations from Various Ports

The National Federation of Pharmaceutical Associations convened a meeting of representatives from pharmaceutical associations of major ports at 6:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Cen Binghuang from the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Trade Association, Dong Bowei from the Shanghai Herbal Medicine Trade Association, Fang Huiqing and Fang Yiyuan from the Hangzhou City Pharmaceutical Association, Xie Zude from the Jiangxi-Hubei Chinese Medicine Research Association, Wang Ziqin from the Anhui Wuhu Pharmaceutical Guild, Cheng Diaozhi from the Nanjing Pharmaceutical Guild, and Gao Jianqing from the Shashi Chinese Medicine Association. Observers included Cai Jiping and Jiang Wenfang, directors of the Secretariat of the Federation; Zhang Shisheng and Cen Zhiliang, members of the Executive Committee of the Federation; Zhang Meian, director of the Organization Department of the Federation; and Ding Zhongying, director of the Economic Department of the Federation (who declared that due to transportation issues, he could not attend and requested notification of the results for consistency. This included five locations such as Hankou City). After the meeting was called to order with the ringing of a bell, Zhang Meian was elected as chairman. The chairman then reported the purpose of the meeting, stating that last year, the Ministry promulgated regulations for the management of drug merchants. Because the Ministry did not fully understand the operations of the Chinese medicine industry, most of the provisions were not in line with the business situation. Drug merchants in various places suffered from the difficulty of complying with them, and they requested that a national conference of representatives of medical and pharmaceutical associations be held to send representatives to Beijing to petition for revision of the regulations for implementation. The Chairman of the National Government granted the request and allowed the matter to be referred to the Legislative Yuan for reference in order to revise them. Now, the Ministry of Health still issues orders to implement the regulations, causing drug merchants in various places to feel uneasy. Letters and telegrams are exchanged frequently, vying for response again. In order to understand the current situation in various places and solicit response methods, the Federation, with the Executive Committee's decision, convened representatives of pharmaceutical associations from major ports to carefully discuss the promulgated regulations, and designated the relevant department directors and executive committee members familiar with the pharmaceutical business to attend and participate in the discussion. Now, everyone braves the summer heat to attend the meeting. I admire your enthusiasm and hope that you will express your great views and discuss the details of this case in detail, which will be reported by the Secretariat of the Federation." Next, Jiang Wenfang, director of the Secretariat, reported on the progress of the case, stating that after the Ministry of Health promulgated the drug merchant regulations last year, drug merchants in various places expressed their opposition. In summary, the reasons and grounds for their opposition are generally no more than the following points: 1. The Ministry of Health lacked the participation of people from the Chinese medicine industry when formulating these rules, so the provisions did not conform to the Chinese medicine business situation. 2. The national health authorities have not yet been fully established and cannot be implemented. 3. The same laws and regulations for Chinese and Western drug merchants are detrimental to one or the other. 4. Management methods abandon the essentials, exceeding the necessary scope, delaying what should be urgent and expediting what should be delayed. 5. Local health administrative agencies lack talent for managing the pharmaceutical industry. 6. The government lacks cultivation and management preparation for the Chinese medicine industry, etc. Therefore, the Federation drafted detailed implementation rules based on the above points to supplement and remedy them, and presented them to the Ministry of Health, requesting adoption to facilitate implementation, but was not approved. Consequently, on December 1, a conference of representatives was held, resolving to request the government to revise the formal management regulations. At the same time, the Chinese medical community also felt restricted by the laws and regulations hindering the development of Chinese medicine, and resolved to gather all cases and send representatives to Beijing to request revision of the regulations in the sub-items. The Chairman of the National Government granted the request and referred the matter to the Legislative Yuan for reference, and the Legislative Yuan referred it to the Legislative Committee for handling. Since the matter concerned laws and regulations, it should be reviewed and approved by the Legislative Yuan, not arbitrarily handled by administrative agencies. The Federation immediately followed the precedent of the Industry and Commerce Law Review Committee and telegraphed the Legislative Committee, requesting the organization of a Chinese Medicine Law Review Committee for detailed discussion in order to achieve perfection. To date, the Legislative Yuan has not held this matter. As far as the files of this association are concerned, the regulations promulgated by the Ministry have become invalid with the President of the National Government's revocation of the laws and regulations restricting Chinese medicine. Before the Legislative Yuan has established formal regulations for the management of drug merchants, there is really no law to abide by. The Ministry of Health believes that if the new law is not born, the old law is naturally effective. The views of the local health administrative agencies are extremely inconsistent. In the current year, local separate regulations are formulated, or local medical and pharmaceutical associations are convened to properly formulate regulations for effective management, such as in Jiangdu County, etc., or separate regulations are formulated in accordance with the regulations of the Ministry, such as in Shanghai City, etc., or the fees are increased compared with the regulations of the Ministry, and pharmacy clerks must pass the examination and obtain a license before they are allowed to engage in the industry, such as in Xiamen, etc. Whether it is legal for local health administrations to separately formulate regulations after the promulgation of the Ministry's regulations is a legal issue that cannot be hastily concluded. However, it is clear that the regulations promulgated by the Ministry are difficult to implement. Drug merchants in various places, except for the first category such as Jiangdu, etc., all express opposition, such as the Shanghai category and the Xiamen category, and request the Federation to continue to lead them. The Federation, in view of the chaotic and unbearable problems of managing drug merchants, had to invite representatives of pharmaceutical associations from major ports to the meeting to discuss together, and also asked the chairman to ask the representatives to express their great opinions, etc. Cen Binghuang expressed his opinion, stating that since there is a clear instruction from the Chairman of the National Government in front and local separate regulations in the back, whether it is effective is no longer a problem. Dong Bowei expressed his opinion, stating that we are not opposed to management and are very willing to have reasonable management regulations, such as the methods in Jiangdu, etc. Fang Yiyuan expressed his opinion, stating that the impediment of the regulations promulgated by the Ministry lies in the same rules for Chinese and Western drug merchants, and those who formulated these rules did not understand the Chinese medicine business situation. In the future, formal management rules must be separately regulated for Chinese and Western drug merchants, and Chinese drug merchants must have the opportunity to participate in the discussion. After the representatives expressed their opinions, they submitted the following resolutions for discussion: (1) Promote a perfect, unified, formal law for the management of Chinese drug merchants (submitted by the Hangzhou Pharmaceutical Association). Resolution: (A) Please ask the Federation to continue to submit the original plan to the Legislative Yuan to expedite the establishment of formal regulations for the management of Chinese drug merchants. (B) Please ask the Federation to notify the pharmaceutical associations in various places to wait quietly for a solution to achieve consistency. (2) This association intends to express its inability to comply with the current management regulations for drug merchants, which are fragmented and obstructive. Please ask the Federation to solicit joint signatures from local pharmaceutical associations (submitted by the Shanghai Chinese Medicine Trade Association). Resolution: In addition to the participating groups, the Federation is allowed to send letters to solicit opinions. (3) How should we proceed if the goal of revising management regulations cannot be achieved? Resolution: (Secret)

Dispute Over the Selection of Chinese Representatives to the International Medical Congress

The National Medical Association's reply to the Medical College of National Central University states: "We are writing to inform you that our members, upon reading the cover advertisement in this year's June 18th Shen Bao and June 19th Xinwen Bao, which stated that 'I, Dr. Luo Aisi, am now going to Copenhagen, Denmark, on behalf of the National Central Medical College to participate in the International Medical Congress, etc.,' were unanimously shocked, believing that international academic conferences originally aim to promote academic exchange and enhance international standing. It seems inappropriate to rely on foreigners to act as proxies. We have always admired your institution as the highest institution of learning in the country, with professors of complete academic character, and believe that you would not waste resources to mislead the public. Therefore, at the seventh meeting of the Executive Committee, it was unanimously resolved to send a letter to your institution warning you to consider the national interest, promote academic exchange, and re-appoint domestic experts. If a suitable candidate cannot be found for the time being, it may be better to abstain from attendance. If a foreigner is sent as a representative, this Association will only send a telegram to the International Medical Congress to deny it. This is entirely the responsibility of national citizens to offer faithful advice and has no malicious intent. Just as we were about to send this letter, we received a correction notice and a letter from your institution on the 6th, denying any such action with strong language and severe reprimands. We are truly apprehensive. However, according to the aforementioned advertisement of your Professor Luo, he claimed to be representing the National Central Medical College in going to Copenhagen, Denmark, while your letter stated that you did not entrust Professor Luo to attend the International Medical Congress in The Hague. Since the locations of the conferences are so different and the statements of the two parties are contradictory, we suspect there is a misunderstanding. Our Association's motion was based on the aforementioned advertisement and was unaware that there was also an International Medical Congress being held in The Hague. Therefore, we did not dare to use the phrase 'irrelevant' in response to your letter. As for the fact that Professor Luo of your esteemed institution, the highest institution of learning in the country, personally declared that he was representing your institution in going to Copenhagen, Denmark, we still adhere to the resolution of the seventh meeting of the Executive Committee and send a letter warning you to clarify within three days whether you will declare the cancellation of the aforementioned advertisement or remain silent. Please provide details and publish them in the newspapers to dispel doubts. Otherwise, our Association will still fulfill the resolution and send the original advertisement and this telegram to the International Medical Congress in Denmark to deny it. We hope you will investigate. Sincerely, the National Medical Association, August 8."

Invented by Doctors Ke and Chen from Southeast Asia

Opium addiction is very difficult to quit once contracted. The Chinese National Anti-Drug Association has always paid close attention to methods of quitting. In the spring, Huang Jiahu, the executive director of the association, went to Southeast Asia to inspect and solicit effective smoking cessation methods from well-known doctors in various places. At that time, Doctors Ke Quanshou and Chen Jinfang, overseas Chinese scholars in Batavia who had been researching smoking cessation methods for many years, recently invented a "Sleep Addiction Treatment Method" that is simple, safe, and inexpensive. Doctors Ke and Chen had tested it at the Yangsheng Hospital in that city. Dr. Wu Liande, a member of the Executive Committee of the Association, and Executive Director Huang had visited and were deeply impressed. Dr. Ke and Chen were specially commissioned to submit a detailed written report of the experimental process, which has now been sent. It is heard that the Association is preparing to have the Association's appointed doctors test the report and decide on the following methods. If this method can be implemented as soon as possible, all kinds of difficulties in quitting addiction can be solved easily, etc. (1) Publish the experimental report of Doctors Ke Quanshou and Chen Jinfang in the English quarterly and the Anti-Drug Monthly, and also introduce it in the domestic medical journals for testing. If the results are satisfactory, publish them together with the experimental process as a separate book to show advocacy. (3) Please ask the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau, the Chinese Medical Association, the Shanghai Medical Association, and major hospitals to test this method and introduce it as much as possible. (4) The Association will contact enthusiastic individuals or groups to establish smoking cessation hospitals to implement this method of smoking cessation and set up training courses to teach this method. (5) If necessary, the Association may invite Doctors Ke and Chen, who invented this method, to return to China to promote it. (6) The implementation of this case should be carried out by the Standing Committee in conjunction with the Secretariat.

Resolution of the Case of Repairing the Tang Pagoda in Western Zhejiang

The Department of Civil Affairs Submitted to the Ministry of the Interior for Record

Construction Has Started in Accordance with Regulations

The Shixing Twin Pagodas built in the Tang Dynasty in Pinghu County, Zhejiang Province, were subject to a demolition and sale issue. Feng Heng, Wu Jingshun, and others jointly telegraphed the Ministry of the Interior to oppose it. Then Shen Songqing and others petitioned the province to change the demolition to repair. However, County Magistrate Fang Li also advocated demolition, which aroused opposition from all the fellow villagers' associations in Hangzhou and Shanghai. As a result, Zhu Jiahua, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of Zhejiang Province, sent personnel to investigate and found that the pagoda was indeed in line with the regulations for the preservation of ancient sites. After returning to the province to report, he ordered the county magistrate to earnestly plan for the repair. However, County Magistrate Fang did not reply for more than ten days. Shen Songqing and others telegraphed the province for instructions. Now, the province has approved: "The telegram has been received. According to the committee's investigation, the county magistrate was previously ordered to earnestly plan for the repair in accordance with regulations. At the same time, the Ministry of the Interior was ordered to approve the record. Please be informed." After receiving the approval, Shen and others invited the county magistrate to a meeting. The county magistrate did not arrive on schedule, and it was generally believed that this was a deliberate boycott. It was decided to follow the regulations and start the repair, which started on the 5th.

Order Tax Offices Not to Obstruct Silkworm Seed

The Zunyi County Chamber of Commerce in Guizhou Province previously requested to send personnel to the cocoon producing areas of Jiangsu and Zhejiang to purchase silkworm seeds and transport them back for seed production for the development of sericulture. When the seeds were transported to Hubei Province, the tax office there attempted to levy a cocoon tax and detained the goods. The Chamber of Commerce reported to the provincial government, which forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance for approval to exempt silkworm seeds from taxation. In addition to ordering the provincial government to order the tax office to release the goods, a circular was issued to all subordinate tax offices to comply with it to avoid obstruction.

Local News

Tears of the Xiang River

Communists Bring Disaster, Homes Destroyed, Families Ruined

A Youth Escapes the劫, Throws Himself into the River

A Sad and Bitter Letter

This time, when the Communists captured Changsha, they burned and killed everywhere, and countless people suffered. It was truly an unprecedented disaster in the capital of Hunan Province. What is recorded in this article is one of the survivors of the劫. Seeing the pain of a family displaced, he attempted to commit suicide by jumping into the river. A Hunanese man named Liu Jin, 25 years old, was a handsome young man who had held an important position in the army. Two years ago, when the troops were reorganized by the Central Government, Liu resigned due to a foot disease and remained unemployed in Changsha for a long time. He was very poor and unexpectedly encountered a Communist disaster. Nine members of his family, men and women, fled on a轮 amid gunfire and shelling, via Hankou, to Pukou. His old mother died on the way. On the 3rd of this month, when he arrived in Pukou, his sister-in-law committed suicide by hanging herself. His hardship was indescribable. Fortunately, he was rescued by his former military commander, Wang Xijun, the current captain of the Capital Security Corps, who purchased a coffin and hastily buried the two corpses of his mother and sister-in-law in the same coffin. Liu then came to Shanghai alone to find a friend but was unsuccessful. Feeling that his life was so miserable, he also conceived the idea of厌世. At about 11:00 AM yesterday, he took a Nisshin Company Anshan Maru ferry from the Wuma Road Pier in the Public Concession to Pubei. When it arrived in the middle of the river, he jumped into the river, hoping to join the波臣. Fortunately, the轮老大, Tang Dexi, immediately stopped the ship and rescued Liu, who was lucky enough to be reborn. He was then sent to the Customs Water Patrol Room. A suicide note was found on his body. After questioning by the chief, the details were learned. Because he had a friend in Shanghai named Liu Jusheng, who currently lives at 44 Chun Geng Li, Qipan Street, Hua detectives Ge Changsheng, Cheng Yongnian, and Huang Songsheng were dispatched in the evening to find him so that Liu could be rescued as much as possible. His suicide note was several hundred words long, detailing his life experience and the various miseries suffered by his family in this Communist disaster and refuge in a foreign land. Although the words were not very smooth, one could generally glimpse the plight of the victims. The words were full of tears and blood and could not bear to be read. It is hereby transcribed below without deletion.

"The suicide, Liu Jin, a native of Hunan Province, 25 years old, from an academic background. Graduated from Changsha City Tenth National Primary School at the age of nine, Changsha Affiliated Higher Primary School at the age of twelve, and Mingde Middle School at the age of seventeen. Because of family poverty, he was abandoned from then on. In the eleventh year of the Republic of China, he was admitted to the Beijing National Army Officer School for half a year, but returned due to illness. In October of that year, he recovered from his illness and joined Cai Junzhang Zhuyou's Tenth Brigade Cavalry Battalion, Fourth Company, in western Hunan as a sergeant. In the twelfth year of January, he was promoted to the third platoon platoon leader. In the thirteenth year, after fighting with Zhao Hengti and being defeated, Cai ordered the entire army to retreat to Longxikou and stop. After being reorganized by He Yaozu, I and others did not follow and went straight to Guangdong to join Sun Zongli's department to assist in the revolution. Unexpectedly, many died of illness on the way due to rugged roads and lack of food. I ran to Guangzhou and took the fourth term of Whampoa. When I was admitted to the school, I had a serious illness for two months. After recovering from the illness, I was introduced by a fellow villager to the First Army, Second Division, Fifth Regiment, One Battalion, Two Company of the National Revolutionary Army as a special affairs chief. In the fifteenth year of June, he was promoted to the captain of the Fifth Regiment's Courageous Squad during the Northern Expedition. On August 3, during the Wuchang Campaign, he suffered a severe gun wound to his left foot. He was sent to Renji Hospital in Shanghai by the military department for treatment. In the sixteenth year of January, his bones were completely healed and he was discharged from the hospital. He was introduced by a friend to the Thirty-sixth Army Special Service Company as the company commander. In July, he was transferred to the military department as an adjutant. At the beginning of January of the seventeenth year, Tang, Li, Liu, Zhou, Liao, Jiang, and others fought with the Central Government, and as a result, they retreated to Xupu and were reorganized by the Central Government. At that time, because my feet were swollen and it was difficult to move, I sold a long vacation and went home to recuperate. Up to January of this year, the family's daily life was incomplete, so I took four old paintings hanging at home to Shanghai for sale, but I was disappointed. I am unfamiliar with the place in Shanghai and have no money. Later, I was taught by someone to go to 44 Chun Geng Li, Qipan Street, Liu Ju Ji to ask for help. I was treated with kindness by Mr. Ju Sheng, who borrowed fifty yuan without setting a repayment date. Later, I returned and heard that on the 27th of last month, the Communists captured Changsha and set fires everywhere and discovered many deviations. I have lived at 157 Banxiang Street, Changsha for a long time, which is on the right side of the Asia Hotel. On the night of the 28th, the Communist fire burned Changsha and my house suffered the same disaster. It happened that my mother was seriously ill and had nowhere to live, so on the 29th, I took a Japanese轮 to Hankou on the 31st to seek help from friends. Unexpectedly, four of my brothers have gone to Qingdao. My third brother died in the Nanchang Campaign. My elder and second brothers work in Yan's department. They have not returned for half a year and their whereabouts are unknown. It is pitiful to abandon my elder and second sisters-in-law and four young children. My wife, Wang, and my mother, a total of nine people, cannot live in Hankou. I had to beg the Taikoo Suiding Ship's comprador Zhang to find a way to go to Nanjing to seek help from Wang Xijun, the captain of the Nanjing Police Department Security Corps (I was his old subordinate), and also ask for work to support the whole family's life. I did not expect that my mother would die on the way. On August 3, I arrived at Pukou and took the corpse ashore together. At that time, there was nowhere to live. Later, a straggler saw the suffering and took me to live with him in Lugia Village in the countryside (this person is from Yuezhou, Hunan). I ran to the city to meet Captain Wang of the Security Corps and talked about all the suffering. Wang raised donations for me and asked me to take the position of sergeant to support the family's life. At that time, because my mother was not buried and the family had no place to live, I replied that I would report later. I returned to Pukou at 7:00 PM that afternoon. My sister-in-law committed suicide by hanging herself. The next morning, I went across the river to Wang's place to continue talking about my sister-in-law's affairs. Seeing my suffering, Mrs. Wang gave me 20 yuan and raised 32 yuan, totaling 52 yuan, and ordered me to return quickly to deal with it. However, the cost of everything in Nanjing is high. A coffin costs 30 yuan. At that time, I had no choice but to buy a coffin and buy clothes, lime, quilts, etc., totaling 47 yuan. I temporarily put my mother and sister-in-law in one coffin and prepared to bury them together, but there was no righteous mountain there. The Lu family gave a great blessing and bought a piece of land one zhang two chi wide for the righteous price of 20 yuan, paying 5 yuan first and returning the rest within three days. I paid him 5 yuan and buried my mother and sister-in-law. That night, I wanted to come to Shanghai to seek help from Cai Junzhang and others. Although I heard that he lived at 3 Ruizhi Li, Muer Ming Road, I had not been there and did not know if I would be rescued if I met him. I wanted to go several times but had no choice because the family had no food, clothing, or shelter, and the land price was not cleared. I wanted my mother and sister-in-law to sleep in separate coffins, so I sold the small spun long shirt I was wearing for 4 yuan and 4 yuan and 6 jiao and 2 fen for a train ticket. I arrived in Shanghai at 8:00 AM on the 6th and ate a meal costing 3 mao. Then I went to Muer Ming Road to look for it but did not find it. I really had no face to go to Liu Ju Ji to ask for help again, and there was no way to return to Nanjing. I wandered around Shanghai City for two nights. Until today, I cannot take care of the whole family mentally. In addition, the environment has been too unsatisfactory in recent years, so I throw myself into the river to die. If the corpse floats, please inform the Cai Residence at 3 Ruizhi Li, Muer Ming Road to collect the corpse to ensure hygiene."

Liu Yulian Gains a Son, Loses a Wife

Liu Han Suffers Injuries All Over Her Body

Liu Yulian, a native of Jiangbei, whose wife, Liu Han, lived at 5 Xiangyun Li, Fen Shui Miao, Hujia Muqiao, North Shanghai, is 24 years old. They have been married for several years, and the relationship between the couple has always been very close. Recently, Han was pregnant with her sixth child. On the previous day, her full term was reached and she gave birth to a child. Liu was overjoyed. Unexpectedly, the parturient woman was frightened after giving birth, causing blood stasis to rise, immediately closing her breath and dying.
